## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillations & dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, time t, and velocity v, which is the standard state-space form for (possibly driven/damped) linear and nonlinear oscillators. Common models include harmonic/anharmonic restoring forces, linear/nonlinear damping, and periodic forcing or parametric excitation in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free simple harmonic oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, no damping/forcing)
- Linearly damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven damped oscillator (cosine form): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (alternative phase convention)
- Pendulum equation (small damping): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (nonlinear restoring torque for large angles)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (nonlinear resonance/chaos under drive)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited limit-cycle oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation via nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear dissipation at higher speeds)
- Conservative anharmonic oscillator via potential gradient: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (general odd restoring series from U(x))
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Time-modulated damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodic damping modulation/active control)
- Nonlinear stiffness + nonlinear damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v - c3 * v**3 (combined material nonlinearity and drag)
- Mixed coupling form (common in identification/control): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * x * v (state-coupled feedback/nonlinear dissipation models)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt is often an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x - c*x^3), so even powers of x may be weak/absent.
- Viscous damping signature: a term -c*v produces exponential decay of oscillation amplitude in the linear regime and is the default dissipative structure.
- Coulomb/friction-like damping: terms such as -c*sign(v) or -c*tanh(c*v) approximate dry friction and create piecewise-smooth dynamics and stick-slip tendencies (if present).
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (backbone curve): adding -c*x**3 (Duffing) makes the effective stiffness depend on amplitude, shifting resonance with amplitude (hardening if c>0, softening if c<0).
- Self-excited limit cycles: negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude is captured by (1 - c*x**2)*v (Van der Pol) or (c - c*v**2)*v (Rayleigh).
- High-speed drag: -c*v*Abs(v) (or -c*v**3) indicates energy loss growing faster than linearly with speed, typical of aerodynamic or turbulent-like dissipation.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t+c0)/cos(c*t+c0) terms imply entrainment, resonance peaks, and possible quasiperiodicity/chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation: multiplying x by a periodic function of t (-(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation and can yield instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Conservative vs nonconservative check: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no explicit t), the system is conservative and admits an energy integral; any v-dependent term indicates dissipation or active pumping.

**GT:** `-0.130179*v*sin(x) - 3.10626*x³ + 0.889089*sin(t) - 0.130179*sin(v)`

Key terms in GT:
1. `x³` term
2. `sin(t)` term (equivalent to `cos(t - π/2)`)
3. `v*sin(x)` term
4. `sin(v)` term

The critical question for each candidate is whether it can represent both `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` with its available basis functions.

**Key observations:**
- `sin(v)` has a Taylor expansion: `v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...` (infinite series)
- `v*sin(x)` has expansion: `v*x - v*x³/6 + ...` (infinite series)
- No finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, or `v*|v|` terms can exactly equal `sin(v)` or `v*sin(x)`

Let me check candidates that might contain `sin` functions:

**Candidate 1:** `c0 + c1*x³ + c2*v³ + c3*cos(c4+t) + c5*v*sin(c6*x+c7) + c8*v`
- Has `cos(c4+t)` → can match `sin(t)` ✓
- Has `x³` ✓
- Has `v*sin(c6*x+c7)`: setting c7=0, c6=1 gives `v*sin(x)` ✓
- For `sin(v)`: needs `sin(v)` but only has `v³` and `v` terms. Cannot represent `sin(v)` exactly with finite polynomial terms.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** `c0 + c1*x³ + c2*v³ + c3*cos(c4+t) + c5*v*sin(c6*x+c7)`
Same issue - cannot represent `sin(v)` with `v³` alone.
Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]

For all remaining candidates (2-16, 18-50), none contain a `sin(v)` term or `v*sin(x)` term. They use combinations of:
- Polynomials in v (`v`, `v³`, `v⁵`)
- `v*x`, `v*x²`
- `v*exp(cx)`
- `v*|v|`, `v/(c+|v|)`
- `v*(c+x)^c`
- `log(cv+1)`

None of these can exactly represent `sin(v)` (an entire transcendental function) with a finite number of such terms. Similarly, `v*sin(x)` cannot be represented by `v*exp(cx)` terms exactly (exponentials of real arguments give hyperbolic functions, not trigonometric).

Let me verify: Could `c3*v*exp(c4*x) + c7*v*exp(c8*x)` equal `v*sin(x)`? We'd need `c3*exp(c4*x) + c7*exp(c8*x) = sin(x)`, which requires complex exponents (c4=i, c8=-i), but constants must be real. So no.
